Welcome Traders

The purpose of this thread is to continue to develop trading rules based on 123 patterns.

In November 2010 I published an indicator called 123PatternsV6. That indicator was the result of much discussion and development work in a thread called [Multiple Trading systems gbpusd only]. Zamanib started that thread and I recognise his valuable work on that project.

The version of 123PatternsV6 that I use is unchanged for more than a year now and can be downloaded from that previous thread.

Download 123PatternsV6

123Alarms addon see post #27
123Alarms update with email alerts post #1286 (7 Dec 2011)

Why a new thread ?

I am starting this new thread to start with a new focus and avoid confusion with that previous multiple systems thread.

Guidelines to keep this thread on-track

This thread's focus is using 123PatternsV6 for trading decisions. 123PatternsV6 custom indicator only No other custom indicators or systems discussed here Any MT4 built-in indicators and chart objects are OK  Any currency pair is OK Any time frame is OK Thread Housekeeping Normal charts only. Go to the previous thread (listed above) for a discussion of rangebar and other charts. Keep posted charts clean and easy to read. Use MT4 File.Save As Picture to create gifs. Use the attachment button in FF post editor to upload gifs and then insert into your post. This way we will not get those huge chart images wrapping the thread off the screen. When quoting someone else delete most of their post. There is no point quoting an entire 50 line post with a one or two line response. Learn how to use the editor properly, quote only the relevant words and cut the rest. Goals

As you know a complete trading system involves much more than somebody's favorite indicator. Risk management, position sizing, timing, trading journals to evaluate progress, entry rules, exit rules and so on.

My goal for this thread is to work together on understanding 123 patterns, when are they useful, and when they are not.

In my posts I will filter out my own 'great ideas' or 'rules' that do not actually support consistent profit making. For example if adding a moving average looks cool/interesting but in reality makes it harder to make profitable trading decisions then it must be removed.

If you have an interest in 123 patterns and would like to work towards these goals then welcome trader, let's do some work.

Robdee

PS Indicator support. Please use the private message system for support questions. Do not post support questions in this thread. Thanks.

PPS Removing rubbish posts. As moderator of this thread I will remove posts that I consider to be irrelevant or just basically rubbish. I know in my naive enthusiasm I've posted rubbish in some threads in the past. I know how it happens. This is a not a personal attack, it is just keeping the place tidy as a learning environment.

--- 帖子 #5 ---
123PatternsV6 uses ZigZag which comes with MT4.

To understand this use a plain chart, add ZigZag only, then go to any candle and look back in time. What are the last three points made by ZigZag? Label those points 1 2 3. When price continues from point 3 to go past point 2 then we have a break. Some people call this 1-2-3-break.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Ideally the move from point 1 to point 2 should be more pips than the move from point 2 back to point 3. In other words point 3 is somewhere in the middle between point 1 and 2. I say 'ideal' because that alignment strongly suggests that 1 to 2 is an impulse move (with the trend) and 2 to 3 is a retrace move (against the trend). This provides evidence of trend direction.

In summary ZigZag filters the noise and allows us to focus consistently on just the most important high/low points. With ZigZag only we can easily observe: previous three price points before any particular candle in time three price points forming a 1 2 3 pattern price retracing from 2 to 3 price trend continuing and breaking past 2 We also have two categories of 123 patterns. First, those patterns where 3 is ideally located in between 1 and 2. Second, those patterns where 3 is located beyond 1. Some would say this second category breaks the pattern and is therefore not a valid 123 anymore.

I prefer to call these two categories ideal patterns and distorted patterns.

Robdee

PS Something to think about - How does the 123-break pattern relate to the popular higher-high higher-low concept, is it the same thing ?

Now about this indicator...

In my first few posts to this thread I am going to start simple and build up layer by layer. This will allow readers to see the foundation ideas that went into this indicator. In the last post I showed that something as simple as just dropping ZigZag on the chart will give you a lot of information.

I think it is important to actually do that. Manually insert text labels 1 2 3 break on to a chart that has ZigZag only. You will get a better feel for what the indi is trying to do. Notice those places where patterns overlap or it is hard to tell the difference between bullish and bearish patterns.

Basic Setup

For a basic setup we keep ZigZag on the chart and overlay 123PatternsV6 on top. We change the indicator settings turning off ShowAllLines ShowAllBreaks and ShowTargets. ZigZag had a default depth of 12 so we set our indicator to the same ZigZagDepth=12.

Now we can see (on top of ZigZag) the blue dots, red dots, and break arrows as below.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

--- 帖子 #17 ---
Welcome AlexM80 Udine Eamonn simmo24 and porfiro, good to have your feedback. Looks like I better carry on with more posts

In the last post I described the basic setup using ZigZag and my indicator. With the basic setup only ideal 123 patterns are shown with red dots for bearish and blue dots for bullish. Distorted patterns are ignored and not highlighted at all with a basic setup.

Now on to the next layer...

To the basic setup I now add sell zones. A red arrow points to the first candle to close below (2). This shows that the bears are strong enough to push the price down and close below that previous price level (2) where the bulls last showed their strength. At this point who is winning, the bulls or the bears ?

The price level where that red arrow is printed now becomes a guide for future selling interest. A sell zone then is an area of future selling interest.

I draw this with a pale green rectangle that covers the red arrow and stretches out into the future. The bears were winning at that price once before so they will remember that price. The bears will be interested in being strong at that price again to sell more lots or to defend their short positions.

The bulls will also remember that they were beaten at that level and will push up to retest the strength of the bears. If the bulls give up that fight too easily then price will drop away too fast and will not come back into that interesting sell zone. In that case I will not have a trade entry which is OK with me.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

For my trades I am only interested in selling when price comes into the sell zone. If I liked I could enter immediately after the break. I could grab some pips that way. However the reason I do not do this is I am usually not watching the chart when that happens (so I miss my chance) and I also like to see some bullish strength (pushing price back up into the sell zone) so I have the bulls enthusiastically filling my sell limit orders (as a result of their buying activity).

Does that make sense ?

Robdee

--- 帖子 #27 ---
A few people have been asking about audio alerts for 123PatternsV6.

There is an add-on called 123Alarms. It can be downloaded from the old thread.

Download 123Alarms

Please note that it does not require rangebars. Just 123PatternsV6 on normal charts will give 123Alarms everything it needs.

The chart must be in the active window (active MT4 profile) for processing to occur and the alarm to activate. If you switch away to a different MT4 profile then the alarm will be mute because that chart is not being processed any more.

You can make your own .WAV sound files to be used with the alarm.

Hope that all makes sense ?

Robdee

--- 帖子 #29 ---
Welcome davidtrader, thanks for your question.

A sell zone is not an exact price line. Rather it is a broad 'zone' or range of prices roughly 10 pips high. I like to think of it as colouring with a crayon. It is not a precise to the pip area, it is a 'zone'.

Use the MT4 menu Insert.Shapes.Rectangle. Start drawing just above and to the left of a red arrow, drag the rectangle down to cover all of the arrow and across to the right to form a long thin horizonal rectangle.

I set the rectangle properties as below

Attached Image

Here is an example of three sell zones at the end of October.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

The most successful sell zones will occur after the bulls have had a successful run up to a new high. They still think they are winning even after the first bearish 123-break. That is when they (the overconfident bulls) are going to push back into the sell zone filling my sell limit orders.

Robdee

PS Support questions about my custom indicators and EAs should not be posted in this thread. Please contact me by FF private message or email.

At this early stage of the thread I am describing the basic ideas that went into the indicator when we were developing it a year ago. These concepts should appear in most any discussion of 123 patterns. Different authors will use different terms to describe what is essentially the same price behaviour and the same analysis. This can be confusing.

What I have been trying to do is use clear and consistent terms that then provide a foundation for our further discussion. If you use the same terms that I do then confusion (in this thread) will be avoided.

Summary of Terms

Terms used in the first four main posts are underlined below.

Using Zigzag only post #5 123 patterns are an important feature of price action Looking back in time you will always see three previous price points Zigzag draws our attention to the most important price points Charts with Zigzag alone provide a lot of information Two categories of patterns, ideal and distorted Basic Setup post #7 basic setup highlights ideal patterns only, not distorted patterns add 123PatternsV6 on top of Zigzag with matching depths turn off ShowAllLines ShowAllBreaks and ShowTargets red dots and arrows for bearish patterns blue dots and arrows for bullish patterns  When are 123 patterns useful? post #14 123 patterns are not always useful 123 patterns are useful in some situations an important goal of this thread is to understand what makes the difference between successful and failed 123-break patterns Basic Setup Sell Zones post #17 Following a bearish 123-break pattern a decision is required about a time and a price for selling An aggressive decision sells immediately after a break (no wait) A conservative decision waits for price to retrace up into a sell zone Consistent sell zone pricing is provided by the red arrow Sell zones are interesting because they are remembered by both bears and bulls as old battle lines Sell zones are useful because they offer buying volume to fill limit orders Sell zones are not an exact price line, they are a small range of prices roughly 10 pips high OK, that is all I can think of this morning. Have I missed anything?

Now is a good time for feedback and questions on these terms and concepts before we carry on.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #34 ---
Spyderman, great questions. You have found a weak area that I was unwittingy being rather too vague about. Thanks.

Yes that is correct. Aggressive entry prices are below 2. The red arrow points to the very first candle to close below price point 2. I see an aggressive entry as the open price of the following candle. Break candle closes, arrow has printed, market order now - no hesitation.

Conservative entries wait for price to break and then move higher into the range above 2 (and normally below 3). This is what the sell zone represents. An area of future selling interest as opposed to immediate selling interest. As the charts show, there are many situations where price action does not return into the sell zone and the conservative entry is not achieved. This can usually be explained by strong bearish pressure overwhelming the bulls.

I'm going to discuss this right now because it is an area of weakness and certainly needs improving. Determining a good price level for the sell zone has been problematic. Last year I tried all sorts of ideas for the placement of the arrows (which act as a guide for the sell zones).

123PatternsV6 prints arrows using the following calculation.SellArrow[shift] = High[shift]+(High[shift]-Low[shift])/3;

In other words look at the breaking candle. Calculate the range (size) of that candle (range=high-low). Divide that range by 3. Add that value to the high and print the arrow at that price.

In effect the arrows are printed above the breaking candle at a variable distance from the candle (1/3 of the candle height).

If the candle size is large then arrow will be further above. If the candle size is small the arrow will be lower. In other words if there is a lot of momentum we expect a stronger pullback. Assuming that the bulls don't give up the fight.
Blue arrows are the mirror image of this. They are printed below the  breaking candle at a variable distance (1/3 of the candle height).

Why am I so interested in sell zones? The reason is I can see a time when I'm going to be searching for liquidity. If I can find a place where the bulls are overconfident and buying into my sell orders for significant periods of time then liquidity will not become a limiting factor.

OK, any more questions?

Robdee

Note: I have been out on my own with this sell zone thing because most participants in the old thread (last year) were using aggressive entries.

--- 帖子 #36 ---
Davidtrader, good to see your chart posting. What I notice right away is your chart is one hour (H1) timeframe. That means the distance between 123 price points is huge, like 100+ pips. Which means in theory that appropriate stops are going to be pretty large too, so as to fit the pattern size of H1.

As a learning exercise I suggest using 5 min timeframe. You'll get a lot more practice because patterns come along more frequently. Plus you will not need more than 20 pip stops operating at that level.

See below my labels on the EURUSD H1 pattern that you posted.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Stop Losses - What I do

Stop losses are best left to personal preference. Your stop management needs to match your own trading personality. However, I will explain what I do.

My approach to stops is to take me out fast if I am wrong. So I simply use a 20 pip stop in all situations. If I haven't selected the right entry price (within a 20 pip margin of error) then I want to be taken out quickly. This clears my mind of the bad trade and allows me to re-evaluate without the emotional pressure of being stuck in a losing position.

Often I will chase an entry down getting taken out at 20 pip intervals until I find a better entry that holds. Although this cuts into profits pretty deeply it is the way I like to operate. That is, keep pruning out bad trades until I find a place where I can "buy and hold" for 100 pips.

Now there are a couple of other things I do with stops. As soon as price moves to +20 above my entry price I move the stop from -20 to breakeven. This means that if price bounces back against me I lose nothing.

When price moves to +50 above my entry price I start trailing pip for pip. This means my stop keeps moving up (trailing) 50 pips below the most recent high. This means if my TP target is not reached I'll still bank some pips.

Hope that helps. Would be good if experienced traders share their own stop loss rules in this thread.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #43 ---
Good question.

123Alarms uses the default setting from 123PatternsV6.mq4

The only way to change that default setting is to edit the code and recompile the indicator. MT4 menu Tools.Metaquotes Language Editor F4 Open the file called 123PatternsV6.mq4 Look for this line
extern int    ZigZagDepth     = 1; Change it to the new value

extern int    ZigZagDepth     = 12; Recompile  I forgot about this because in the old thread we were using rangebars and ZigZagDepth=1 was best setting for constant rangebar charts.

Robdee

To download 123Alarms see post #27

--- 帖子 #44 ---
This post shows the same basic setup with one more layer added.

I call this layer Fibo Targets.

Fibonacci retrace tool is used to draw one fibo with five levels configured at 0.0, 0.5, 1.0, 2.1, and 3.8. The fibo is always drawn starting at price point 2. The fibo is then stretched out to price point 3. If that looks too small then I drag the fibo further out to price point 1.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

This is the only variation I use with the basic setup. Start drawing at 2, drag to 3, if that is too small, drag to 1 (instead of 3). So the fibo's dotted line will always show on the chart as linking either 2-3 or 2-1.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #47 ---
Hi simmo24, the dots identify price points that make up the 123 pattern, arrows signify the 'break' part of the pattern. A decision to buy or sell depends on all the factors including things like timing and previous price action.

In the next version of 123Patterns I will not be using arrows to highlight the break candles. I will use some other method that does not seem to say 'buy here' and 'sell here' like arrows do. Arrows tend to make people think, "OK time to trade" which is not right.

In the chart that you posted you have not switched off ShowAllLines and ShowAllBreaks therefore you are seeing arrows that are not associated with ideal 123 patterns. In other words you are seeing arrows that are associated with distorted 123 patterns. The basic setup I have been explaining requires ShowAllLines=false ShowAllBreaks=false ShowTargets=False ZigZagDepth=12.  Dots show only the 123 price points for ideal patterns  No dots will show on 123 price points for distorted patterns  Arrows point to the first candle closing beyond #2, the start of the break  Does that answer your question ? hope so.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #49 ---
If there are no coloured dots when the arrow appears this sounds to me like ShowAllBreaks=true which allows break arrows to show on distorted patterns. Distorted patterns are not well defined and it is possible that an arrow could be printed only to be erased again after more price action pushes the ZigZag price points further out. I have seen this occur.

It is also possible that you are using ShowAllBreaks=false and there is some kind of repaint problem with the indicator that I am not yet aware of. I switch MT4 chart profiles quite often which means my indicator displays are being refreshed often so I certainly could miss something like the repaint you describe.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #57 ---
My general rule is placing the buy limit orders inside the buy zone.

In the chart you posted there is a problem because some candles are closing below 3. That is bearish. So, in that specific situation I will not be trading an uptrend because those bearish closes mean the bullish 123 pattern is no longer valid.

Attachment

Another way to look at this is to oberve the poor quality of the break. Yes one candle closed above 2 but then the very next candle closed below 2. There is no follow-through on the break so it is not good quality. When I see this it makes me suspicious that it is a fake-out not a break-out.

As a forex trader, what data can I ignore?

More specifically, when looking for trade setups, what data can be ignored? This is a question I asked in a poll last year. Many traders have many systems and various rules. However most of them can agree on a few categories of data that can safely be ignored.

Which ones do you think can be ignored?Time of day (eg London Open, London Close)

Volume and changes in Volume

Wicks on candles (upper and lower)

The range of candles (high - low)

Patterns (channels, triangles, waves etc)

Technical analysis 'news' posts on FF news page
Or to put this another way, what data should not be ignored?

--- 帖子 #63 ---
Sure will do. Remember the reason this thread exists is to develop the ideas further from what we were doing a year ago, hence the title "123PatternsV6 revisited".

Sell zones and buy zones are well described in this thread. That is how I find and enter a trade. It is also becoming clear to me that the 123-break is most reliable during times when there is greater than average liquidity.

No other technical inputs, no use of any oscillators or moving averages. That guy who was using CCI(200) was on H4 charts which doesn't suit what I'm trying to do. I don't understand how he proposed to trade that.

On M5 I'm only looking for small intraday swings so expect to TP at +50 and +100, not much more than that.

This thread is pretty wide open in terms of developing the art of 123 pattern analysis. If you know some technique that improves our ability to make profitable trading decisions (and it's not some other custom indicator or EA) then you're welcome to post it here.

Robdee

Nice post spacePip, I'm not sure what you mean about avoiding price bars, do you mean 'constant rangebar charts' which yes I am avoiding those. In a rangebar chart all the bars are the same height but their time durations are variable.

The chart you posted is an 'M5 bar chart' that simply uses bars (instead of candles) to represent the same OHLC values for each time period. In my mind there is no difference between that and an 'M5 candle chart'.

If you are able to explain a brief summary of the Ross Hooks approach (or post a link to an existing summary) that will be appreciated. Looks like it provides a very specific entry criteria which may be useful.

The last post I made on the main topic was What data can I ignore ?

In that post I referred to a poll I have been running asking traders to select multiple categories of data which they think are safe to ignore as they evaluate trading setups.

What is the least important data available to us? More than 60% selected Technical analysis 'news' posts on FF news page. Yes, safe to ignore, I certainly agree with that. I don't even read those TA 'news articles' because they distract me and play with my mind.

By contrast the most important data (that cannot safely be ignored) according to traders are these two:
The range of candles (high - low) Patterns (channels, triangles, waves etc) Only 15% voted to ignore these two. In other words 85% are saying these two categories of data must be included in the analysis.

OK, patterns I can understand, we use all kinds of patterns. This thread is all about one of the simplest and most common patterns out there. I agree, patterns must not be ignored.

Now what about the range or size of candles. The number of pips from the top of the candle to the bottom. From the highest bid to the lowest bid during that time period. Is a 30 pip candle telling us something different from a 10 pip candle ? No I don't think so.

It is all just OHLC isn't it? Seems to me the Close is the important thing. So why are 85% saying we can't ignore range? Maybe the way I worded the question has biased the answers, I don't know.

Sorry i rushed the post didn't make it clear, I didn't mean rangebars, I was simply referring to normal chart candles/ bars and whether you are keen to use them with this method, or are you just sticking to the plain chart with only the zigzag indicator?

If you are open to using candles or bars then the Ross Hooks could be of interest as a way of entry when price retraces back into your buy/ sell zones.  Basically a ross hook is described as "the first correction following a breakout of a 123 high/ low" so this is similar to what you are looking for.  Entry is triggered with a break of one of the correcting (retracing) bars.

There is lots of free info on the internet about this if you google joe ross and im sure a thread on here somewhere, but the following pdf explains it well

This style of analysis, comparing bar-by-bar is what I call price action. Any chart style, tool, or indicator built into Metatrader is OK in this thread. What I am against is getting wildly off topic discussing various custom indicators and EAs.

Observing the price action within a buy/sell zone using Ross Hooks and TTE gives traders a defined price and time for action. That final prompt, "see price has dropped below the last retracing bar, you are good to sell," may be that small extra edge of confidence needed to take appropriate action.

Not being a chart-watcher I will find it difficult to catch exactly the right TTE moment on a live chart. However I will illustrate past RH/TTE price action in some of my future chart postings.

--- 帖子 #83 ---
Welcome PartyPips, good question. Just before I answer that take another look at your 123 numbering. 2 is always in the direction you expect the price to move. So for a bearish pattern 2 is the always the lowest number. For a bullish pattern 2 is always the highest number.

OK, yes there was a candle that closed below the bearish point 2 (that you label 1). The problem was the red line coming from that point did not stay intact. This is a side effect of using ZigZag to find the price points. I accepted this limitation during last year's development but it did cause concern for those trying to catch absolutely every possible break.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Here is an example of a distorted bearish pattern where the red line coming from point 2 did remain intact. It remained intact long enough for a candle to clearly close below it. That is what 123Patterns is looking for to print the red arrow.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

Traders please note this is an advanced setup that I have not yet described anywhere in this thread.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #86 ---
Hello all,

I just want to comment how do I trade using ZigZag:

About Equity Management & Risk to Reward Ratio:

I'm sure that this is one of the most important when trading.

Usually I only risk 2% of my account and go at least for the double of the risk. So, why I don't care and why I do care about stop loss in pips:  I don't care because I will be risking 2%, it doesn't mater if the stop loss is 10 pips or 40 pips from my entry I will increase or decrease the lots to trade, and it will represent 2%. I do care, because if my stop loss it's 10 pips I will go for 20 pips (my minimum target will be the double) but if my stop loss it's 40 pips at least I will go for 80 pips, and for my it's much easier to take 20 than 80 and in both cases I will earn 4%.

Why at least the double, because in the worst case if I'm only right 34% of the time I will be positive .

About Entry, Stop Loss and Exit:

Entry: I do trade Ideal & Distorted patterns but I ALWAYS wait for a retracement using A- level off broken support or resistance (label #2) (the arrow at the indicator it's a good guide) or B- Fibo levels with the combiantion off candlesticks formation (the best ones: bullish or bearish engulfing and evening or morning star, and I also look for tweezer top or bottom and pin bars, nothing else)

Important: if I don't have a new 123 pattern I will reentry in the same direction

Stop Loss: 3 pips the high or low of the signal candle or the previous candle.

Exit: Fibo targets 1.618 for retracements to 61.8% and 1.27 if the retracement was around 78.6% or just double the stop loss as target (i do this usually for the first and the second trade of the day "if" i'm planing not to work all day, but if the 2 firts trades are looser, them I keep trading using fibos target).

NOTE: once I set my target I don't follow the market moving the stop loss. It's like set and forget

Drawdown: 4 loosing trades in a row could happen in a single day, but you will recover it with fibo targets very fast,  and yes, i had 5 and 6 loosing trades in a single day but they are not common

Aditional Indicators: don't need it, 123 pattern it's all

I will be posting some trades and you will see how it works.

IMPORTANT NOTE: this is my way of trading from some years ago, but great that Robdee has post the indicator to help new people.

Any question, just let me know.

Happy thanksgiving day

--- 帖子 #90 ---
hey i do not know if this will help but.. the zigzag draw lines at and in between extremes of price action. the defining factor in when or why a line is drawn is when price is greater then stated percent value.

the depth is referred to as the minimal amount of bars that has to be drawn before the indicator is looking to draw a new line, thus creating lines in between a specified interval of bars.

the third value that the zigzag uses has to do with the amount in pips that differs from the last point of the line. by definition, if this amount is exceeded a new line is drawn.

i might have got something wrong though.. but if you or anyone else for that matter has any questions regarding this please do not hesitate to pm me. thank you

--- 帖子 #96 ---
An odd enhancer is picking the setups that give the best probability of success

Note the 2 setups on  EUR .

The first setup had a weak move away from the level and price did not move far from the breakout. Result was 1-2 the small 14pip move

Granted a round number 1.3300 was in the way of the trade

The second setup had a strong move from the level and price moved a fair distance before retracing back.

A strong move away from the setup arrow implies a strong supply area (more sellers than buyers) which if price moves back too ,there should be more sell orders there. Result was the 1-2 approx 75 pip move down.

Didnt take this trade was asleep nz time just for educational purposes

--- 帖子 #117 ---
Hi Rob

First of all best of luck with the thread.

The distorted pattern is a 2b trade, just google that and you'll see them clearly. They are the same general concept as double tops/bottoms and 1 2 3 trades i.e. a sign of test and failure at a key level. I don't trade all 2b i.e. distorted pattern trades, much more selective.

Personally I feel once you have had the first 1 2 3 to change direction then you have a series of HH, Hl's and they are the same as 1 2 3's.

Paulus I think it was did some great work re 1 2 3's coming out of Asian session into London. The idea of only taking trades counter to the direction from Asian session. This would take into account the notorious London open head fake concept avoid some losing trades and hopefully get into the main move of London session.

Trading 1 2 3's at your zone prices is a very important concept, perhaps easily explained as support becomes resistance and vice versa.

What else, I am very wary of taking (what I describe as) weak 1 2 3 moves very early in US session that counter the London direction. Often those small 1 2 3 patterns will fail and US session moves back into the London direction (often with a distorted pattern).

All the best.

--- 帖子 #118 ---
OK your other comments about not bogging down the thread with nice to have indi's.

The trend is your friend, that old adage applies for a reason, well because it works. The consideration then becomes what do you use to describe as your trend. A very personal decision for many.

MTF analysis then becomes important. One of the prolific EA writers at FF includes a standard option to take signals when the D RSI is below the 50 level. Thats a pretty good rule of thumb.

Will this mean that some trades are missed when the D chart is turning, of course but should save many losing trades going against the D trend.

How you get by avoiding losing trades on the odd counter daily trend days I have never figured out (as far as an EA goes), manually you can just avoid selling as an example on 5 min chart after a strong D hammer.

--- 帖子 #119 ---
There are various indi's around that highlight SR levels, drawing lines at the identified levels. I've never used them but I'm sure they would assist.

I almost hate to say it but its so simple. An 8 lwma after a retrace gives an easy visual of a 1 2 3. The red line is the clear buy zone/resistance became support. A positive close candle moving through the 8 lwma with little/no upper  wick (for a buy) avoiding candles that are overly large (15 pips or so)  is a method I've used for years.

Also in this case the D has had a nice positive close and approaching (but not above its 50 RSI). Interestingly to put above posts into context. Price came out of Asian session lower so after a positive D close look for buys.

How you code this goodness only knows.

--- 帖子 #129 ---
Hi Frank

Perhaps a fine line here between going off topic and Robdees request to help fine tune 1 2 3 entries.

Bias is D chart based, if you are going against that its one of those counter trend choices. You either accept the risk as being higher, perhaps lower your profit expectations (grab lower pips if in profit), or pass on the trade.

Pls see above posts, we take certain 1 2 3 trades on 5 min if its in line with D trend without waiting for 1hr to fall in line. For example if (as has been the case now except the last day or 2) the GU, eur trend is down you are looking for sell opp's. A classic would be price moving higher out of Asian session we would not be looking to buy but waiting for a 2b/dble top/1 2 3 at the recent extreme of price that you are hoping is in a sell zone at an important level.

If you miss that initial 1 2 3 trade at the recent price extreme then we would be looking to only trade after 1hr/4hr has lined up. In the case of a sell we would be looking for some kind of hesitation candle (on 1hr) eg doji, shooting star, close in lower half of candle OR 2 or more candles that are pos closes but fail to break higher out of the recent range.

Long explaination of your question but waiting sometimes for D 1hr trend to fall in line is a solid way to trade.

--- 帖子 #130 ---
Personal view is roughly 70% of the time pa will follow the D chart from 1 day to the next. Thats decent odds, you then need to say where will you get in. It might mean that if trend is down London might try and buck that and needs US vol's to turn market to fall in line with D. Bottom line you can STILL lose money if you are trading trend IF you are using small stops and NOT being careful with your entry.

1 2 3's is a classic method to use to shake out efforts to go against the trend.

--- 帖子 #142 ---
If the market is turning there are often a couple of days when the big guys turn off the sells, the rest of the market is still selling. IF this is a turn the big boys will start buying, they can't buy all at once they have too much ammo. So a turn will often have its own D 1 2 3 (with rsi divergence for those that watch it). We haven't seen those patterns yet.

You traded a big pic 1 2 3, make your candles much bigger and you'll see the smaller 1 2 3's. IMHO after your entry there was a distinct 1 2 3 lower high which might have given warning of a failure to move up and you could have gotten out with a smaller loss, or IF you believe the market IS turning you'd need stop below the D's low.

As Rob has mentioned we could easily be headed lower looking for a D dble bottom, 1 2 3 high before the move up really begins.

First of all a little story. Islander a superb trader, I asked him how he did so well trading 1 min time frames at certain specific times of day. He said 10,000 hours of chart time. He was looking back all the time to perfect his entry requirements and his methods.

Moving on.

Trend (and therefore ranging markets) are time frame dependent, what may be ranging on 4hr might give great opportunities on 1hr/5 min. Looking at the chart post 135. The market hasn't had a real pullback on D chart yet, no real 1 2 3. As some pullback is likely still I would look at the distance from high to low for that trade, the market has moved a long way to take an entry there on what is not yet a confirmed upward trend.

Just my view, until trend is confirmed up on D chart I would be looking at lower time frames for opp's to get entries much closer to turn points.

G'day Glenn, welcome to the thread. Those 5min settings you are using are the same as my basic settings I use on 5min and 4hour. I expect that those settings will also work fine on 15 min and 1 hour. At least as a good baseline. I did a lot of tweaking last year trying to find better settings but never found anything more reliable than those defaults.

ZigZag=12 makes sense on 5min because 12 candles = 1 hour.

ZigZag=12 makes sense on 4hr because 12 candles = 48 hours.

--- 帖子 #154 ---
hey and welcome to the thread :-)

i would just like to comment. i do the same on entry, see the break of point 2, watch for the TTE zone and have orders there to take me in at that point.

however i do calculate the distance of TP differently. taking the distance from point 2 to point 3 as the target, from point 2. as such if my TTE zone

equals rr 1:3 or greater on that trade i will take it.

example: TP is 30 from point2, TTE zone says i risk 15 until point 3 then that is risking 15 to get 45 hence 1 for 3.

if the case is that my TP is greater then 30 as point2 would be another value then i consider that as an even greater opportunity and strongly consider moving my target even further, as per always keeping my 1 for 3 mentality. greater is only bonus though, hope you understand this :-)

as for the part where it does not always work i do this; if the cci(200) is > 100, on long side in this example, at the point 2 of the 123 pattern then that point 2 is acceptable. if not then it isn't. this thinking can be applied differently with other indicators set to other numbers. it is just something i've found to be working for the moment and it is only my interpretation. i think somebody wrote about it in this thread also, though i cannot find it atm.

// meatball :-)

--- 帖子 #187 ---
Vantage is correct in saying that the arrow prints after a candle closes beyond price point 2. The indicator is always looking back in time at the last three price points to see if they make a valid 123.

Valid 123 patterns may later be rendered invalid by price action that exceeds the bounds of the original 1 2 3.

Also, distorted patterns (ie ShowAllBreaks=true) leads to redraw/repaints at times.

See previous posts on this topic... Arrows and distorted patterns Post #49 123 setup becoming invalid Post #1113 These are known limitations and are all being taken into account with the next version V7 which is currently in testing by myself and another trader.

Vantage suggestions for fine tuning entry options are appreciated and will be added in V7.

The logic used in V7 will not be complicated. It will be less complicated than V6. The logic for finding and acting on 123 patterns will essentially be the same as Vantage's recent posts.

I have a solid and proven EA code base so it will not be difficult to build an EA for this.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #196 ---
Vantage, emb

Your recent charts and discussion are very helpful, great work!

I see three options for aggressive entry before the break of point 2.

1) Vantage's candle that closes with very little wick (ie not much opposite pressure) and occurs after price point 3 and before price point 2 has been broken. This provides a consistent approach to aggressive entry.

2) emb's entry line "50% between 2 and 3" providing better R:R ratio and another consistent approach to aggressive entry.

3) My favourite, "50% between 1 and 2" followed by preparing to exit/reverse on 210% (aka Fibo Targets).

See the case study that we have all been posting from 6 December...

--- 帖子 #202 ---
Traders may like to do some V7 beta testing?

I am very busy this week so I will just post this and then carry on with my other work for a few days.

New ideas... V7 focuses on aggressive entries, it does not wait for the break. Filters are used to avoid too much chaos CCIFilter prevents buy entries when CCI grossly overbought (smoothed cci > 125)  CCIFilter prevents sell entries when CCI grossly oversold (smoothed cci < -125)  VolFilter prevents all entries when volume is below average. Below average volume is defined as MA12(fast) < MA144(slow).  Attached Image (click to enlarge)

See the attached template v7betatest.tpl that shows how the default filters are configured.

This allows you to visualise the filtering process.

Note: Alarms and a trading EA are planned but not yet built.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #230 ---
Version 7 is a work in progress and I seek to add ideas that may improve it.

I believe it is critical to identify the LL, LH, sequence using fractals.

I have added the fractal zigzag to the chart to help illustrate what I believe are the more important 123 patterns. The fractal zigzag is a guide only, but a useful one.  It is not perfect.

To me, the critical 123 patterns should be based on LL, LH, fractals and I have shown that sequence on the chart. So these particular LL, LH, locations are based on fractals.

I did not add the fractal indicator as it clutters the chart. With a bit of practice you can easily locate fractals on your own and establish the LL, LH, sequence.  Same withe fractal zigzag, the human eye is much better at locating these things, but indicators help with the learning curve.

Price rises to probe the down trend line and then falls back to make a 123 pattern that I identified with black numbers.  Point 3 is a pullback of 50%. The Fibonacci projection (green) is used on my black 1 2 3 (fractal) points to calculate a 161.8 target which is 1.3 pips away from the 50% entry.

Version 7 locates so many nice 123 patterns but if we could have to option of locating 123 based on fractals I think it would add a powerful component.  I believe it could filter out a lot of the confusing situations.

Identifying the LL, LH, sequence on the fractals (and HH, HL, in a bullish trend) is very powerful.

Can it be done with zigzag, fractal zigzag or another way altogether?  I am not a programmer but if it can be done, I think that adding 123 fractals to the method would worth exploring.

My two cents worth.  Please look at the attached chart.

--- 帖子 #235 ---
I have made changes to the 123PatternsV7 beta code.

Option now exists to show only Bulls or only Bears.

Used when trader has decided market is trending and does not want to see opposing entries.

To hide the Bulls set ShowBulls=False     (eg in a downtrend)

To hide the Bears set ShowBears=False  (eg in an uptrend)

Inserted Code Notes           = "BETA TEST EURUSD M5 Setup"
ShowBears       = True
ShowBulls       = True
ShowStatus      = True
ShowDots        = False
VolFilter       = True
VolMaFast       = 12
VolMaSlow       = 144
Other changes: ZigZag is gone! This is what was causing most of the repaint issues. CCIFilter is disabled, Have not seen much benefit in this filter. Status for time of entry, price of entry, pips moved above/below Status for daily range, average daily range, and DR/ADR ratio Status for ratio of last candle volume compared to average volume See attached file below version 20111214 and the matching template.

--- 帖子 #239 ---
Hi davidtrader, yes you are correct.

V7 signals show both lines (buy and sell) coming from the body of the signal candle.

The idea here is suppose you have a sell signal and then later price breaks above the buy line. This is a good time to close the short and maybe change to a buy. (instead of just waiting to get stopped out)

Another way to think of the two lines is a sell zone. As long as price does not close above the sell zone then it remains valid. If two candles close above the zone then it is broken - no longer valid.

When this occurs the sell zone often becomes a buy zone. (resistance becomes support)

Hope that answers your question.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #247 ---
Hi sako, thanks for your feedback. I'm always glad to hear a different point of view. I have been putting so much effort into overcoming ZigZag's repaint issues that I have been overlooking the merits of ZigZag. Yes it does have merits.

Another indicator I have written uses ZigZagDepth=8 and it appears to be a very effective level of filtering. I also agree with what you say about higher TFs that is why I use V6 on 4 hour chart.

The higher the ZigZagDepth number the more little insignificant peaks are filtered out. This allows us to focus our attention on the larger, more significant, more powerful price points.

How much filtering is appropriate?

This is always problematic, some people want to see every possible trade highlighted on their screen. Others are happy seeing only a select few high probability trades. I am in the latter group, so very selective filtering is my usual preference.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #249 ---
This happens when I release Beta code.

People ask me, why are you still using the old version ?Answer: I have been using the old version for a long time, I know it works.
Answer: The new beta code is for testing only. It needs to be tested over a period of 2-3 months. It is just a development tool for new ideas. It is like playing with stuff to see how it works. I do like the look of it but I am not very confident about it.
Are you wondering which version to use V6 or V7 ?

Keep in mind that V7 is beta test only, I have no idea how  consistent it will be over the long term. The focus of V7 is on early  aggressive entries (before the break of 2) so this is not really following strict 123-break  methodology.

V7 seems to fit the last few days of price action by  passing a large number of potential entries through a series of  filtering rules. It seems to fit because I made it fit. Only a few of those many potential entries make it  through the filters and are displayed. (If you want to visualise this  filtering set ShowDots=True). Now we need to wait and see if it continues to perform without me doing any more fitting.

V6 is my tried and tested old faithful 123-break indicator that  has been around for more than a year. You can control the level of  filtering with ZigZagDepth and if you can put up with a few ZZ repaint issues  then it will suit many applications.

Final note, if you cannot clearly identify 1 then 2 then 3 with 2  pointing in the direction of the trade then it is not 123 analysis, it  is something else.

Hope that helps. I get frustrated when I post Beta test code and some people start treating it like a production release.

Maybe I should call it Alpha code for testing, I don't know.

Anyway, enough said.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #277 ---
Welcome Halba, good questions, yes I agree there are longs, if I had more confidence in the bulls I would have been buying right on the 50 fibos. I use V6 dots to draw the fibos from point 1 to 2. I then look for price action to show respect to the 50 fibo.

With V7 beta there will be times when the entry shows before the break of 2. That is OK, that is how it is designed. Just need to make sure that all three points are visible 1 2 3, then V7 painted candle, enter the trade. It is also OK if the entry appears after the break of 2. The R:R will not be quite so good but it is still a valid entry imo.

I gave up trying to get the indicator to number the dots because there is so much overlap, bulls vs bears, and true vs distorted. This means it is actually better for the operator to figure out where the 123 price points are. I label them manually as the intraday chart unfolds. V6 gives a good hint because it drops coloured dots on the more obvious 123s.

Hope that helps. Trade well.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #284 ---
Option 1 (more safe) 1 2 3 break (red arrow) draw fibo 1-2 now place order on 50 fibo  Option 2 (safe) 1 2 3 (no wait for break) draw fibo 1-2 wait for Vantage signal candle (small wick) now place order on 50 fibo  Option 3 (more risk) 1 2 (no wait for 3) draw fibo 1-2  now place order on 50 fibo Note: 123PatternsV6 will not show the 123 dots until the break has happened. So either you find your own 123's (eg with ZigZag) or you wait for the break. V6 makes Option 1 easy.

--- 帖子 #296 ---
If you are already using 123PatternsV7 then you may be interested in this..

123AlarmsV7 Immediately after 123PatternsV7 paints a signal, 123AlarmsV7 plays a WAV file. There are options to show popups or send email messages.  This alarm system requires that 123PatternsV7 is installed. See post #235. Here is the code... (see MQ4 file attached at end of post for download)

Inserted Code //+-----------------------------------------------------------+
//| MT4 CUSTOM INDICATOR                     123AlarmsV7.MQ4  |
//| copy to [experts\indicators] and recompile or restart MT4 |
//+-----------------------------------------------------------+
//| Free software for personal non-commercial use only.       |
//| No guarantees are expressed or implied.                   |
//| Feedback welcome via Forex Factory private message.       |
//+-----------------------------------------------------------+
#property copyright "Copyright © 2011 Robert Dee"
#property link      "www.forexfactory.com/robdee"

#define INDICATOR_VERSION    20111217       // VERSION 1 - compatible with 123PatternsV7 indicator only
#define INDICATOR_NAME       "123AlarmsV7"
#define RELEASE_LEVEL        "Public"
#define MT4_BUILD            409

#property indicator_chart_window

extern string Notes           = "Alarms for 123PatternsV7";
extern string AlarmSound      = "symbol";  // WAV files must be in MT4\sounds folder, set to "symbol" to use audusd.wav etc.
extern int    AlarmRepeat     = 6;         // number of times to repeat the sound
extern int    AlarmDelay      = 10;        // delay in seconds before repeating the sound
extern bool   AlarmPopup      = True;      // true means popup is enable, pops once per alarm
extern bool   AlarmEmail      = True;      // true means email is enable, email once per alarm

int      alarmcount;
double   alarmprice, emailprice;
datetime alarmtime, lastsoundtime, lastcandletime;

//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
//| Custom indicator initialization function                         |
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
int init()
{
if(AlarmSound == "symbol") AlarmSound = Symbol()+".wav";
} // end of init()

//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
//| AlarmArrows() process the alarms based on indicator arrows only
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
void AlarmArrows(double buysig, double sellsig)
{
string msg;

// BUY SIGNAL
if(buysig != EMPTY_VALUE && sellsig != EMPTY_VALUE)
while(buysig > sellsig)
{
msg = Symbol()+" BUY "+TimeToStr(Time[0],TIME_MINUTES)+" "+DoubleToStr(Close[1],Digits);
if(AlarmPopup == True && alarmprice != Close[1]) {Alert(msg); alarmprice = Close[1];}
if(AlarmEmail == True && emailprice != Close[1]) {SendMail(msg,msg); emailprice = Close[1];}
// sounds
if(alarmcount >= AlarmRepeat) break;                 // do no more
if(TimeCurrent() < lastsoundtime+AlarmDelay) break;  // do no more
PlaySound(AlarmSound);
lastsoundtime = TimeCurrent();
alarmtime = Time[0];
alarmcount++;
break;
}

// SELL SIGNAL
if(buysig != EMPTY_VALUE && sellsig != EMPTY_VALUE)
while(sellsig > buysig)
{
msg = Symbol()+" SELL "+TimeToStr(Time[0],TIME_MINUTES)+" "+DoubleToStr(Close[1],Digits);
if(AlarmPopup == True && alarmprice != Close[1]) {Alert(msg); alarmprice = Close[1];}
if(AlarmEmail == True && emailprice != Close[1]) {SendMail(msg,msg); emailprice = Close[1];}
// sounds
if(alarmcount >= AlarmRepeat) break;                 // do no more
if(TimeCurrent() < lastsoundtime+AlarmDelay) break;  // do no more
PlaySound(AlarmSound);
lastsoundtime = TimeCurrent();
alarmtime = Time[0];
alarmcount++;
break;
}

return;
} // end of AlarmArrows()

//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
//| Custom indicator iteration function                              |
//+------------------------------------------------------------------+
int start()
{
double buysig = iCustom(NULL,0,"123PatternsV7",2,1);   // use value from last closed candle (shift=1)
double sellsig = iCustom(NULL,0,"123PatternsV7",3,1);  // use value from last closed candle (shift=1)

AlarmArrows(buysig, sellsig);

return(0);
}// end of start()
123AlarmsV7 indicator

All my indicators are free for personal non-commercial use.

All I ask is that my copyright is respected.

Private messages are the best way to send feedback to  me about the  indicator. I don't want this thread to become a indicator  support forum thanks.

123Alarms must be in the active profile to be processed and  trigger the alarm.

Three WAV files in sounds.zip are extracted to MT4\\sounds  folder, you can also make your own WAV files but they must be saved in this  folder. Download sounds.zip from post #1224

--- 帖子 #301 ---
Welcome Zeb_Sailor, yes that is the question!

They are all valid 123's, so which one is the right one for drawing the fibo.

As you say, while the structure unfolds (live in real time) it is not easy. We should keep an open mind and keep updating our fibo when new price points appear. It becomes a bit of an 'art form' which neither I nor my maths based indicators have mastered yet.

First the ideal setup

1-2-3-break (all four steps visible)

NOW draw fibo from 1-2 and look for retrace to 50%

If a good reaction to 50% (no candles close below it)

then I have high confidence in reaching 210% and 380% targets

Observe reaction to first target

If price action breaks through easily (complete candles on the other side)

then it makes sense to hold on for second target

Second the non-ideal setup

1-2 (only two steps visible)

now draw fibo from 1-2 and look for retrace to 50%

(same sequence as above)

Use a ZigZag or fractals indicator (or 123PatternsV6) if you need help spotting the price points.

Hope that helps.

Robdee

--- 帖子 #323 ---
Ultimately 123 is an attempt to use the Elliot Wave structure and could really be numbered zero, one, two, to make it compatible.

We should start at fractal zero.

We have a wave to a fractal at one.

A wave back to another (opposite style)  fractal at two.

Then we try to catch the third wave ... if price moves past one again.

We only know for sure that a third wave  is in progress, when price breaks past the fractal at one.

However, we can gain extra pips if we make an act of faith and enter between one and two and are then correct about a pending break, past one, taking us into Elliott wave three.

(Different strategies for entering between one and two could probably take up their own thread; Fibonacci ratios, reversal candle patterns and spread cost calculations being being amongst them.)

Maybe this is a chance to rename the traditional 123 to zero one two.    It would certainly clarify what this is versus what the conventional 123 was and also integrate it seamlessly into the Elliott Wave.

Elliott Wave is a tough subject, but parts of it are easy enough to use. Renaming 123 to 012 would somewhat harmonize the two where they overlap and take advantage of the knowledge available in both camps.

--- 帖子 #330 ---
Ok, a slightly different approach. Not using the larger fibo targets and filtering the trades using the v7-dots. No other indicators attached, plain v7. Besides that, I think one should make sure which sessions to trade.

I was looking at the thread again last week after being of for a while. Mid december I posted some charts with the first v7 release. During the holidays I have looked at it again, but as movement and liquidity is poor and unreliable, any outcome during this period should be neglected. So, last week I started things up again with the current v7 version and today I decided to give it a shut.

I like to draw lines, simple lines from dot to dot, fractal to fractal (not using fractals myself) or using Demark lines (in most trading I use this). This will filter a lot of signals out. As Robdee said in this thread that (about the v6 arrows) not all arrows should be seen as direct trade signals, but that they should be filtered.

As we can choose to display the dots in v7, I use this for drawing lines. For an up-line (breaking down): connect the last/current blue dot with the prior blue dot that was below the current blue dot (just as TD-lines, Demark). The other way around for down-lines.

Now I need my aggressive 123pattern signal to close below/above the trendline break. This means AFTER the break, within a few candles. When a signal comes first, then followed by a trendline break and I still can get in, I won't. First the break, then the signal (the signal candle can break the line as well). Stop is at the last dot high/low (=+spread). Target is at R:R:1. This is not an ideal situation in most systems, but.... As it's the aggressive version, the goal is to grab this instant movement, collect some pips and get out. In my other trading I use a more conservative RR, I am not a gambler! In another thread I have learned that jurn_e makes a nice return by doing just so, collecting short run's. For this aggressive version I think such an approach could work.

I made my first live trade this morning. In the chart it’s the second trade that I marked. The first one I missed. The first trade gave me a nice 11pip, now see what happens in the coming week. Will keep you posted.

--- 帖子 #359 ---
Last one for today +20pips. Didn´t take the signal straight away because of the news. Used the 100% expansion for the TP.

txfx. It is not rocket science, put the Oscillators on a chart then mark the signals with a vertical line. Do the oscillators agree with the signal. Is there divergence. Does everything agree, if not then pass and wait for the next one. Look at the first signal, LH edge of the shaded area, BRN very near, Oscillators in OS and possible Bullish Divergence, is this a good short signal? Just repeat this exercise for each signal. It significantly reduces the number of losers.

--- 帖子 #369 ---
Let the chart tell you where price is going, Looking Left, will give you clues. But if in doubt, 123 patterns follow Market Harmonics CD = AB.

I also use the premise that if price pulls back (Leg 2 - 3) to 38% Fib then it is likely the expansion will reach the 161.8% Expansion unless there is something bigger in the way like a major S&R Level, like wise the pullback to the 50% Fib is likely to expand to the 127% Expansion.

I have attached 2 charts for todays trades, they should make it more obvious.

--- 帖子 #374 ---
They are part of the Trading Made Simple method and show when the Green Line crosses the Red line on the TDI indicator. They are a little sensitive and sometimes show when the lines just touch rather than cross, so you always have to check visually. On the larger TFs they would actually signify a Trade entry point.

--- 帖子 #386 ---
These should help.

1. 123 Chart Pattern + Fib expansion. Sunil Mangwani. Concentrates on the 123 Reversal Pattern. My Favorite for the most pips.

2. 123system. Mark Crisp. His emphasis is on the HTFs and stocks but the concept translates to the LTFs and Forex very easily.

3. TTE Traders Trick Entry. Joe Ross. Earlier entry on the 123, but use with caution. Great in a trending market but can rip your pants off and throw you to the ground in a Ranging market.

--- 帖子 #424 ---
the 123patternsv7 indicator repaint?

--- 帖子 #425 ---
They are 123 points, you will probably have noticed by now that the 123 Indi does not identify all the 123s, and I do not choose my trades based on the indi, I choose my trades based on what 3 time frames are showing me. The fact that my trades coincide with the 123 Ind just goes to show how good it is. As for how I determine my TP, I do not use the Fib Expansion In isolation. I hope the attached chart explains it. I look for Confluence of Fibs & S&R where price has been before, is price reacting to the fib levels. That is how I determine my initial TP, if another 123 forms after my entry I measure the Expansion and see if it agrees with my initial assessment. If I have missed the entry for a larger 123 I measure the expansion from the previous formation. I base this on the fact that the larger the 123 formation is, the more relevant it is because it will also be visible on the Higher Time frames so more traders will be reacting to it.

--- 帖子 #437 ---
Last loser was here. http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...62#post6706262.

I used to have lots of losses, years ago, I believed the crap that losses are part of trading and you should accept them, but I wasn´t making any money with that attitude, now, I do not like losses!! I close for B/E or a small loss, if I have to, and then re enter if price turns and continues. I see no need to hold a trade until my stop loss is hit, I actually think that  that is one of the most stupid things to do in trading. If my entry is wrong, I get out.

If you pick your entry correctly there should be no need to take a loss.

I never ever let a winner turn into a loser.

I like the 123 entry off Support or Resistance because price will move far enough to guarantee a profit or at least a safe exit.

I limit myself to no more than 2-3 trades per day, reduces my exposure to risk and reduces the chance of an impulse trade. Unless I am feeling playful.

I have learned to be patient and wait for right setup.

I pass on trades that I am not 100% confident about.

--- 帖子 #543 ---
To answer a multitude of questions, simply, I have copied this from Nial Fullers site, this is the link to the full piece. http://www.learntotradethemarket.com...rading-signals. His emphasis is on the Daily, but he concentrates on just a few simple PA strategies that are easy to identify and to act upon and the beauty of this is, it transfers to the lower time frames. But, you just have to remember that any lower time frame signal is less reliable than one on the HTFs.

This is the meat of it.

"
The “big boys” know how to filter their trades

If you’ve fallen prey to thinking that the “big boys” are trading a hundred times a day and day trading until their eyes bleed, you’re mistaken. Many of the guys with big money wait on the sidelines patiently and “pounce” only when the best signals, levels and trends are present on their charts. You need to learn to think like the big boys, act “as if” you’re a “player”; be intelligent and stop using the market for entertainment and start treating this as a real business.

The best and most logical explanation for why you should trade less is because there are inherently less good signals for any strategy or system; think about it…the reason a signal is high-probability is because it doesn’t happen extremely often, if it did then it wouldn’t be a high-probability event would it? If you force yourself to trade all the time you’re going to be taking a large quantity of useless and second-rate signals, this is simply a waste of your time and money.
Creating a filter checklist for you trades

A good exercise for any trader is to create their own checklist of different filters that they use to scan the markets for potential signals. You can just create a quick checklist with one to three sentences describing what the filter is and then an example image of the filter under it.

Here’s an example filter checklist that I’ve created from the examples above (in yours you would place an example image below or next to each sentence like the ones above but maybe a little smaller):
1. Look for a signal with a protruding tail that creates a false-break of a level. Watch for obvious protrusions and false-breaks of key levels in the market. This filter can be applied to trending markets or to counter-trend trades. Wherever you have a key support or resistance level, keep an eye out for false-breaks / protrusions of that level.
2. A long-tailed pin bar is a high-probability pin bar. Long-tailed pin bars work very well in trending markets and as counter-trend signals, as we saw in the examples above. A long-tailed pin bar is always something to keep an eye out for when analyzing the markets.
3. Don’t “bet” on a breakout…wait for confirmation instead. A good filter to use for tempting looking breakout trades is to wait for the breakout and close above or below the level. Then, the breakout is “confirmed” and you can start looking for a signal in the direction of the break. This will help you avoid many false-breaks, especially in range-bound markets.
4. Look for continuation signals after a pullback to support or resistance in the trend. Trend continuation signals are a ‘bread and butter’ strategy that you need to watch for.Watch for trends and then retracements within those trends, then keep an eye out for signals forming from “value” areas that indicate the trend might resume.
5. Don’t trade signals in tight “chop”. Be cautious trading pin bars or other signals that form in thick and choppy consolidation. If you see two or three pin bars in a row as in our example above and the market is not coming off in the direction implied by the pins, it’s an indication that it’s probably not going to come off. We need to see momentum and a clear breakout from consolidation before entering from a signal formed in “chop”.
6. Look for “confluence”. Watch for obvious “hot points” in the market, or areas where two or three or more levels are intersecting…these are very high-probability levels to trade from.
7. Avoid signals that form in “no man’s land”. This one is sort of the opposite of the confluence point. If you see a signal that just looks like it formed without any type of confluence and looks like it’s just placed wrong, you should probably avoid it. This filter is especially important to use on the 4 hour and 1 hour charts.

Whilst having things like checklists and an overall trading plan are very important, they are only one part of finding the best trading signals. The man or woman doing the analysis and pulling the trigger is JUST as important as the strategy or trading plan they are using.

As traders, we need to develop our subconscious “gut” trading feel on an ongoing basis, learning from the charts and keeping notes and simply immersing ourselves in day-to-day market analysis and observation (note I didn’t say immerse ourselves in ‘trading’). This helps us develop a good intuition and gut feel which go hand in hand with a good trading strategy."

Hello, Dee

Thanks

Justin

--- 帖子 #593 ---
Short answer. No. The TDI indicator is made up of a Smoothed RSI and is therefore no more reliable than any other indicator for ascertaining Divergences. My preference for Divergence is the Stochastics, this is why I have it on my charts. Others will tell you the CCI, RSI or MACD etc. It is just a matter of preference and the settings used, I have used Stochastics for years on the setting 8,3,3 and have found it to be an extremely good indicator of divergences on the time frames I trade, it also shows me what stage of the price cycle we are in.

The only way for you to decide which you prefer is to put a couple of them on a chart and make a direct comparison. Do a search on the web for alternate settings, many traders just use the default settings without realizing that those were the optimum settings when the indicator was first devised, since then then the market has changed.

2. Divergence on 15m/1H (optional).

3. Candle formations (Double top/bottom, 123break pattern).

4. Patterns must be off S/R zones such as fibs of last days swing low-high, and BRN.

5. Must be going from oversold/overbought to opposite.

6. Candle must close before entering trade.

--- 帖子 #674 ---
Patience is a virtue, but combine that with knowledge and your losses will diminish. It is one thing to be a great technical analyst, but sentiment is also a powerful short term driver of the markets!. As day traders we need to be aware of the sentiment as it can move the market in the opposite direction to the technicals. Here are 2 reports that can help you, I have posted these before, but my daily pre trade routine is

1. Read and download the Danske Technical Update and the Danske Daily Update.http://www.worldwidereaction.com/smi...work/7_6_8.gif

2. Check FF Trading calendar for timing of News.

3. Open my charts check the sentiment against technicals.

4. Make Pips.

Hope it helps

--- 帖子 #678 ---
Yesterday I took one trade EU +20. It was an excruciating trade that took 3 hours for just 20 pips. The 123 looked good as it was combined with a Triple top off Resistance and justified an early TTE entry, the 161.8% Fib Exp only gave 20 pips but initially it looked like it would get there quite quickly. I identified a Daily S&R at 1.3180 and put my TP there, but 3 hours later we were coming to the end of my trading day and price had still not gotten to the 161.8% exp, so I moved my TP up to the 161.8% and settled for 20pips. Had I not intervened it would have been 35pips as price did make it down to the Daily S&R.

Lesson for the day was. "Do not bugger about with your TPs, set it and leave it!!" If in doubt trail your stop!!

--- 帖子 #713 ---
I did not take this trade, I am some what lazy monday mornings. However, it does provide me with an opportunity to show you how you can use another pattern along with your 123, to determine the most likely place to take Profit. In this instance it is a Pennant pattern. PDF attached explaining the Pennant.

The 1-2 leg formed as part of the LO Fake out, the 2-3 leg pulled back to the TL Base of the Pennant, the early entry would have been as price broke thru the top of the Pennant for the second time, this would have given a 45 pip trade, the standard entry on the break of point 2 would have given 35ish pips.

There are a number of clues as to where price was likely to go. The confluence of Daily S&R and 50% fib & previous area of Resistance just a little lower.

Confluence of the 161.8% Fib exp and BRN 1.3200, this would only have given 15ish pips.

Using a measured move, Market Harmonics, this would have confirmed the most likely TP area was the confluence of Daily S&R, 50% Fib and previous Resistance.

--- 帖子 #725 ---
You have to change to V7 for an updated alarm. or. change "zigzag depth" from 1 to a higher number, Robdee the originator actually used a setting of 12. But you also need to remember that the alarm on V6 was an early warning, if you want an alarm as the arrow forms to indicate the cross of the 2 point youre entry will be late, which depending on momentum might only be a couple of pips to 10 pips or more.

An arrow without dots means it's a distorted pattern. It means it's not exactly how a 'perfect' 1-2-3 pattern should look like, but it's close to it.

Please also see robdee's answer to a similar question in post no.49

http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...07#post5155407

--- 帖子 #799 ---
You hit the 200, you just needed to draw your fibs in the right place. Plus, look for the S&R levels these will give you confirmation of your TPs. Price will go to the S&R levels more often than it will go to the 200, why? Because the S&R level is Factual, price has been there before and thousands of traders are viewing them, the 200 level is a theoretical level that is only observed by people using it. In this instance the 200 was a good level for TP because it was close to the S&R level.

--- 帖子 #842 ---
EU +44 +70.

GU +50 +100

"Focusonmoney" See the lines on my charts, see what price level they are at, now draw the same lines on your chart and scroll back, what do you see happening when price hits the line. Practice looking for levels, after some time it becomes much easier. Start on the Daily, then change down to the 4Hr, then to the 1Hr. Use the 1hr and 15min for your short term S&R levels. Another way is zoom out, you will see the levels much more easily, they actually become obvious when you zoom out.

Or take a smaller position size, one that does not hurt so much

--- 帖子 #854 ---
I do not have many MAs. Using the TEB method, 100 EMA 30 EMA 5 EMA. On my EU charts 50 EMA 200 EMA. I only use the 200 EMA as a potential target because so many pro traders have that on their charts and it usually forms S&R because of this. If an ema is part of confluence, then yes it is a target or it is part of the target. Any other time I TP at or near an MA it is coincidence and there is usually another more pertinent reason for taking profit in that area.

--- 帖子 #859 ---
When does Price hit the Session Day´s High or Low??. Do you care?? As Day Traders you should! If I need to explain why then you should not be reading this.

Here is a link to Thomas Bulkowski´s site where he conducted a study, the results are interesting. Bare in mind this is stocks, the results will be slightly different for Forex and for each pair, but it is not difficult to do a simple back test. Remember you need to test the times when you are awake and trading so that the results are relevant to you, to often I see backtest results covering 24/5, fine if you are an algorithm that never sleeps.

http://thepatternsite.com/IntradayHighLow.html

Also interesting

http://thepatternsite.com/studies.html

And

http://thepatternsite.com/CandleEntry.html.   and   http://thepatternsite.com/Hammer.html   and  http://thepatternsite.com/ShootingStar.html

and   http://thepatternsite.com/BearEngulfing.html  and  http://thepatternsite.com/BullEngulfing.html

--- 帖子 #863 ---
Yah, I like Pin Bar at support or resistance, it looks pretty much reliable , also other forms have a better probability at that area.

--- 帖子 #864 ---
The reason I used this site as an example is because he is one of the few Analysts who has actually done the research and listed the Success and Failure rates for candle patterns, too many people talk about candlesticks and Patterns as if they were a foregone conclusion whereas the reality is very different!!! The Pin Bar on it´s own only signals a reversal 59% - 60% of the time, however Bulkowski did not test the Pin Bar at S&R levels had he done so he would have found a significant difference in the predictive success rate! So you are correct in choosing the Pin Bar (Reversal Bar) at S&R.

Bulkowski´s analysis of a 123 Pattern, although different to how we use it, he uses a trend line in the pattern, shows that this pattern confirms a trend change 73% of the time. My own analysis in Forex, puts this figure at closer to 86%.

http://thepatternsite.com/123tc.html

His analysis of an ABC correction (Measured Move) is closest to our 123. But he actually Analised each leg of the Pattern and evaluated the success rate of a 100% expansion. Check out the "Measured Move Up Trading Tips"

http://thepatternsite.com/mmu.html

"The measure rule predicts a price target! This works 83% of the time in a Bull market and 93% in a Bear market

http://thepatternsite.com/PatternReview5.html

--- 帖子 #911 ---
EU. +77 +50 +60 +50 +30 +25 +35 +30

EJ. +60 +60 +55 +7 +25 +50

My trades for the week. Due to the market I had to depend on S&R, 123 and TDI so there are a mix of entry types on the charts, for that reason I have not explained the entries on the charts, but most of the entries were 123 & S&R combinations.

I have found an interesting sessions marker which includes Total pips for each session. I normally trade from 9 - 5 GMT +1 and I found it useful to know how many pips were in each session rather than total daily pips, it helped provide a more realistic expectation of what I could expect to gain each day as a Day Trader. If I was Swing trader then that knowledge would be irrelevant.

To set it up just enter your session start and end times based on your broker times, eg. My broker is GMT +2 so my session times are 10.00 - 18.00.

F8 on the chart and select "show object descriptions" to show the session pips.

When scrolling back you may get some elongated session boxes I found that changing TF and back again easily fixes that, the thread I found the indi on said refresh the chart but that did not work for me.

Enjoy

--- 帖子 #913 ---
If you mean do I ever get stopped out for a loss, Rarely, Look at EJ 25th Nov, 1st trade, I closed for only a 7 pip gain this was a counter trend trade and it looked to me like it was reversing back into trend so I closed it. 2nd trade I re-entered following a 123, I targeted the BRN 137.000 which was short term S&R but Stochs went down to OS so I adjusted my TP back to the congestion area just to the left.

Looking at the 2 charts do you see any reason why I would have taken a loss?

Another reason is, I do not over trade, look at the charts, I am averaging 1 trade per day, I have plenty of time to make the decision to trade.

It was not always like this, I used to lose loads and then spend twice the amount of time getting it back, the difference now is I "Never" let a winner turn into a "loser", I have been trading the same pairs with the same method for years and I have learnt to pick my targets and leave it alone unless PA tells me otherwise.

Hope it helps

--- 帖子 #919 ---
The 123 indicators that are available are good for training your eyes to recognize the 123 patterns, but I do not rely on them for trade entry signals.

If you look in the attachment section you will find several PDF files that describe entry and exits rules, TEB63 had a thread about the 123. which I can recommend.   http://www.forexfactory.com/showthread.php?t=106165

You could also read "this thread from the beginning", RobDee the thread originator put in a lot of work to explain the method.

http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...mentid=1259832
http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...mentid=1222510
http://www.forexfactory.com/attachme...mentid=1207459

It's always so easy to see, from your charts and reasoning why you chose your entries and your exits. But hindsight is a wonderful thing. In real time, it is a struggle to see so clearly what to do, and I feel, or more importantly, what NOT to do.

How did you decide to pay attention to one S&R level and not another?

I ask because many times, I think price will more further and it doesn't. And other times, I think price won't move further and it does!

--- 帖子 #929 ---
Stop looking at 5 min charts unless you are only planning to scalp for 10 pips! I gave up even looking at 5 min charts some time ago, what you are seeing is noise and misinformation.

I follow the 1hr chart and use the 15min to fine tune my entries. and/or as an early warning system.

I draw my S&R levels off the Daily & 4 hr. 1hr & 15min have minor S&R levels that I want to be aware of because this is where price stalls for a while before carrying on to the HTF S&R levels.

For news trading I trail my stop aggressively. For standard trades it depends on PA but I usually just aim to get to BE + 2-3 pips and give the trade some room to develop, if price stalls for some time I tend to move sl up under the consolidation zone.

Sorry but I do not have a list of rules that I follow, I am a Discretionary trader and follow what PA is doing.
