--- 帖子 #941 ---
OR, you can try, 32, 50, 200 EMAs. OR any other combination of numbers, at some point price will hit those MAs what ever the number that you chose. Some people chose MAs set to FIBO numbers, it really does not matter, What does matter is how many traders are watching a particular MA, take for instance the 200 MA this by all accounts is an important one for the Swing trader and 1,000s of swing traders will make a decision based on this MA.

SMA, EMA, Hull MA, Stevensons Rocket MA or the Dead Cert MA, on the Higher Time frames it does not really matter what the MA is called. Many of the variations of MAs were developed to try to provide an edge on the lower time frames so their sophisticated calculations are more or less irrelevant on the higher time frames.

--- 帖子 #942 ---
You can use what ever MA or any other indicator you prefer.

I simply use the 34 Hull MA because I like it, it's my line in the sand, I check to see if price is above or below the 34 HMA on the W1 and D1 charts and then look for 123 patterns on the H4 to enter a trade in line with the higher TFs trend.

It's nothing new, it's not rocket science, I do it because it works for me.

I don't have time to watch the charts all day, trading H4 charts with pending orders means I have time to do other things and not get burned out.

--- 帖子 #1004 ---
A Pin Bar is only a Pin Bar when one of the following occurs and the bar does not form within an area of consolidation

Pin bar + divergence at the tip of the reversal bar

Pin bar + clear Support or Resistance

Anything other than this is likely to be a Hammer, a Hammer often occurs within consolidation and is a signal that price will reverse back into the initial trend. An example of all three is attached.

--- 帖子 #1025 ---
No. You trade with the stop loss you can afford and you place that stop loss at the time of your entry, it is called a "stop loss" for a reason. PHx62 and Eeelfranz used an emergency stop loss of 50 pips, that is what they could afford, others place stop at the last swing high or low, even if that is 70 pips it all depends on your money management, but one thing is certain, what ever your stop loss, it is put in place as soon after your entry as possible. A few tears are preferable to opening a vein.

Have a good weekend.

--- 帖子 #1053 ---
Hi Dee,

EU was in prison for the past few days and today was just released.......

You may noticed that Meta trader is automatically updated on any restart for build 600 , I noticed that the platform gets stuck and freeze for many times, I started to debug and see what could get wrong, at last I found that whenever the platform starts it tries to load the 123 indicator, during that loading it hangs for a while and for some reason it's related to Zigzag depth that is used with 123 indicator , after many tries and a lot of working around I ended up removing the 123 indicator and everything worked smoothly with the new update, I already recognize the 123 pattern visually and it's not a big deal to use the indicator for.

I just wanted to share this with you as I know that you may face the problem.

waiting to see you after the NFP tomorrow....Good luck

--- 帖子 #1083 ---
Found this on another site and I hope it helps with the indicators here.

As a result of the recent MetaTrader 4 (MT4) Build 600 upgrade, and subsequent versions, the folders for saving EAs have been moved.

To identify your MT4 build click Help > About on your client terminal

https://ci3.googleusercontent.com/pr...014_075902.png

Since this upgrade EAs, Indicators, Scripts and Library files are now to be saved in different locations.

You can access this folder from your MT4 client terminal by clicking on File > Open Data Folder.

All indicators should be saved in the folder titled: MQL4 > Experts.

All indicators should be saved in the folder titled: MQL4 > Indicators.

All library files should be saved in the folder titled: MQL4 > Libraries.

All script files should be saved in the folder titled: MQL4 > Scripts.

Clients using an earlier MT4 build, please note that once you upgrade to the new version your EAs, Indicators, Scripts and Library files will be transferred automatically to the folders mentioned above. Please ensure that this is effective once you upgrade and that your EAs and/or indicators are working correctly.

Finally, the MQL4 language has also been modified in this latest build, and this may interfere with your installed Expert Advisors (EAs) and indicators. If you notice any issues with your pre-installed EAs or indicators we encourage you to take the below actions.
Action 1: Contact your EA provider if you do not have the source code available and request an updated version of the EA, or ensure that the current one can properly run under the new MT4 build.
Action 2: If you have written your own EAs or have the source code available, please follow these steps:Navigate to Tools > MetaQuotes Language Editor – a new window will appear. Navigate to View > Navigator – the Navigator box will appear in this window (if not shown already). Double-click on the EA/indicator you would like to use and update – the relevant EA script will appear in the main window. Alternatively navigate to File > Open to locate the relevant EA/indicator source code saved on your computer. Click on Compile in the toolbar on top of the main window (or navigate to File > Compile) – a message will appear in the Toolbox window at the bottom. Once this has completed and there are no error messages displayed you will need to close and reopen your MT4 client – your EAs and indicators should now be ready to use If errors or warnings are displayed please review your code again or consult an MQL4 expert. If it is an EA you are using, it may be good to back test it again, and/or run it on a demo environment for a while prior to using it live.
FinFX wants to inform our clients that we do not upgrade to latest version of MT4 until it has been fully tested on by our development team and with our technology providers.

Build 509 will be usable as long as MetaQuotes keeps the build available for login. Currently the oldest supported version is build 500 and according to MetaQuotes this should not change meaning that even after we have upgraded our server to the latest build, clients can still use the old build 509.

Feel free to contact our Customer Support team via live chat or email [color=#0066cc]info@finfx.fi[/color] for further assistance.

The video is 2.13 hrs long but it is only the first 1.5 hrs that matter.

--- 帖子 #1163 ---
nice trade Dee, don't you think that trading the FOMC is a little bit risky ? I mean I saw many cases for FOMC that the price would just wobble up and down hitting buyers and sellers at the same time , do you trade little amount at that time or it's pure news trading ?

--- 帖子 #1164 ---
You have to judge sentiment and how the market has been prior to the announcement, in this instance the market had been in consolidation with little or no direction, sentiment was that tapering would continue, foregone conclusion really, so even just confirmation of this was likely to move the market in favour of the Dollar add to this the projected rate announcement and the direction was guaranteed, all that was left was to work out by how much.

I can not understand why so many experienced traders advise not trading the news, probably because they have not learnt "how" to trade the news, in reality it is no different than ordinary trading it requires exactly the same skill set and preparation, I actually find it much easier to do. For some years I traded nothing but the news, it was great, get up late have a leisurely breakfast do a few odd jobs go to the bar have a Cafe Americano and a Bocadillo con Pechuga de Pollo discuss the weather with some of the old fellas, return to my office at 14.15pm ready for the announcement at 14.30pm, by 15.30 I was done with 50 - 100 pips in the bank. When the bar installed WIFI I would take my laptop there and trade from the bar, the view over the valley is much nicer from there.

--- 帖子 #1165 ---
Good to know that you are trading the news while relaxed, I bet that this didn't came by chance, I know people got a stroke or even got part of their stomach removed before they decided to quit trading the news.

I see the problem with how each trader could interpretate the news or decide the sentiment , each trader has his own understanding and tools , with the fact that in many cases the market would react exactly the opposite direction to what the news really came out, add to this the herds reaction when someone falls you start to see the whole domino follow that fall.

someday I will be trading off the beach relaxing like you do and hopefully we can have a drink together.

Cheers

--- 帖子 #1206 ---
Hi, sorry I have taken so long to respond. I generally place my SL a couple of pips below/above the 3 point unless the pullback to 3 was so deep then I place my SL below/above the 1 point. I am looking for a 1:1 RR minimum and a minimum return of 30 pips, if I can not see at least 30 pips potential I do not take the trade. Determining Targets is a little more difficult to explain, i go thru a process of assessment. Look Left, S&R levels Major or Minor, BRNs, Fib expansions, Trend lines, previous consolidation (part of S&R) but most of all I am looking for the strongest area of confluence. I do this before entering a trade (important) because i want to know if there is any point in hanging around waiting for an entry. I normally highlite these areas on my charts that I post. When do I move to B/E? Depends on PA. When do I use 2 TPs? Depends on PA and what obvious potential stalling points there are in between my entry and final TP.

In addition, you may have noticed that I use the stochastics oscillator, I have done so for many years. Why?

here is a description from "Stockcharts.com chart school. I found their explanation to be the simplest and most logical.  http://stockcharts.com/school/doku.p...tic_oscillator

"Developed by George C. Lane in the late 1950s, the Stochastic Oscillator is a momentum indicator that shows the location of the close relative to the high-low range over a set number of periods. According to an interview with Lane, the Stochastic Oscillator "doesn't follow price, it doesn't follow volume or anything like that. It follows the speed or the momentum of price. As a rule, the momentum changes direction before price." As such, bullish and bearish divergences in the Stochastic Oscillator can be used to foreshadow reversals. This was the first, and most important, signal that Lane identified. Lane also used this oscillator to identify bull and bear set-ups to anticipate a future reversal. Because the Stochastic Oscillator is range bound, is also useful for identifying overbought and oversold levels."

Attached is a PDF "George C Lane Stochastics" he explains how to use the stochastics.

Attached File(s)   George C Lane Stochastics.pdf

59 KB
|
5,493 downloads

The reason I am including this information is, far too many traders use indicators that they actually know very little about. To them it signals an entry and that is it! They do not understand how! so therefore are not aware of the pitfalls of each indicator or the benefits of understanding the lesser known nuances.

Watch this space for an explanation of the BOSO method ( buying the overbought and selling the oversold) using the Stochastic.

--- 帖子 #1281 ---
I can not add any thing to what you have said other than to compliment you on your understanding of what is happening.

However.

I do have a "contentious" opinion about Price Action. And I must emphasise that this is just my opinion. I do not expect you or any one else reading this to have to agree with me.

Price reveals the intention of the market prior to any other thing, does it? Every thing else lags behind price! Absolutely true. "Everything" does lag behind price.

Think about it, where is price on a chart? it is to the far right, there is nothing else beyond it,  it is the thing that moves a pip at a time, that is the actual price.

The next thing we see on a chart is the result of this price movement. Individual Candles, Individual bars, What are these? "Indicators", of what "has" happened.  How long does it take for one of these indicators to complete? are they ahead of Price? No. What they do is form recognizable Patterns from which we make a decision.

How does this differ from what is happening at the bottom of our charts?

But what we are seeing at the bottom of our charts is "Lagging"!!

The only thing that is lagging is the individual traders ability to understand and interpret what they are seeing.

This is a very simplistic explanation of my opinion, in reality a whole discussion (argument) could be had but it is not one that I will participate in because agreement would never be reached. There will always be differing opinions and every one is entitled to theirs.

Attached is an example of how an indicator in combination with other things helped me make the decision to take a reversal and how for me, the indicator pattern "predicted" the reversal.

I started my trading career with e-mini S&P 1min chart, I eventually found that to be too slow for me and I discovered Tick Charts and started trading 89 Tick charts as you can imagine this was extremely exhilarating and not at all profitable I thought the problem was that the e-mini S&P was too brutal so I started trading the mini Dow & the mini Russell as well, still using Tick charts. If you are not aware Tick charts are the equivalent of Super Turbo Charged formula one cars, they are fast! The 1min chart looks like an old banger in comparison. Trading the Dow and the Russell did not make me any more profitable and I started the quest for the "System" that would save me. This went on for 2 years and then I worked it out, the rest is history.

In essence, you are right. But I would not recommend  any trader tries to scalp the ES with out first having traded Higher TFs. The main reason many traders start on the ES is because it is a highly liquid instrument and you very rarely if ever never get filled even during news time, slippage is also low because of the sheer volume of orders going thru.

--- 帖子 #1358 ---
Just a reminder.

The Best Times To Trade the Forex Market

Basic stuff I know, but some times we pass on the obvious because we are looking for the more complicated.

Attached Image

There are times in the market that regularly produce trades on a consistence basis. You will witness volume at these specific times.2am EST: The German open. This begins the day, and breaks the slow choppy price action of the Asian session. 3am EST: The London open. This is often the exact reversal of the German open 8.00-8.30am EST: 90 minutes before the opening bell begins the attempt into the gap fill for the open.(Futures) 10am EST: Most big money will wait for the first half hour after the bell to place their first trades of the day. The 10am time frame produces more entries than any other. 11.30am EST: 30 minutes before the European close. This is called the 11:30 reversal period, the beginning of the daily doldrums. We usually witness profit taking in the opposite direction from whatever the main direction of the morning was. 1.30-2.00pm EST: The end of the daily doldrums. This is many times a stop run from the consolidation of the slow choppy lunch time trade 3.30-3.45pm EST: An attempt at a run toward the daily pivot for the next day. Stick to these specific times and you will find yourself in the beginning of trends as they develop, normally!

A word of caution.

Remember we are in the summer doldrums, now is the time to adjust not just your clocks but also your Pip expectations. What was a 5 minute 10 pip scalp will now take 2 hours or more. So put aside your frustrations and accept that these are leaner times and do not enter a trade just because you feel you should be in the market.

If you want your local time here is a link to an app. http://www.forexmarkethours.com/markethours.php

--- 帖子 #1444 ---
Some thing for the weekend, sir.? Where to take Profits? it takes time and practice to see where price is likely to go and until you have the experience there is a way to "guess" more accurately, both methods shown on the chart have also been illustrated in the 123 Trading PDFs that are available. Price has a tendency to create patterns and because of this we can project where price is "likely" to go,

The Measured Move.

We are using the 123 pattern so we use the formula that CD is likely to be equal to AB. AB is the 1 to 2 leg, CD is the 3 to D leg.

There are 2 methods that can be used,

The Fib Expansion Tool, this is the true CD=AB because the price expansion is measured from point 3 (C).

The Normal Fib Extension Tool, this is not the true CD=AB because the price expansion is measured from point 2 (B).

(before you ask, I have used both methods and have no particular favourite, I use the "200" method most, but I could not tell you why).

When using either of these methods look for confluence, this will help you asses the viability of the move.

Use the Measured Move to determine if a trade is actually worth taking, is the Risk to Reward worth the aggravation.

When and if you do a search for more information on The Measured Move, do not be confused by the ABCD Pattern, this is an entirely different trading pattern.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

This chart shows the Fib settings.

Just got around to watching this video. So, the advice when news trading is to look deeper into the news release to discover things that could move the currency in a different direction to what is expected. So you get the economic release and you have a little read, then you look at the chart, oops, it's already moved 100 pips. What I suspect is happening, is that people who pay for early news data, get wind of the extra detail and pile in, leaving everyone else on the wrong side of the trade.

Using the 'news gun' on forexpeacearmy is my preferred method.

"Retail traders, don't sell yourself short. What we looked at as far as technical, charts, fundamentals, etc is pretty much the same thing that you look at as well. The Spot guys would always talk about highs and lows and support and resistance. Some would use that to "run stops" (meaning getting the price to trade that level to uncover s/l loss orders in order to make a few pips. So be careful where you put your stops, the bank traders will gun for them if they can!!!! Also, there was never any Hedge Fund's that did anything you and I wouldn't do, if eur was selling off because of Draghi's comments they sold like the rest of us only in size. Don't be impressed with Hedge Funds at least when it comes to the spot market. They don't know anymore or are anymore sophisticated that you are, its just a matter of degree. I give you another example, the biggest FX fund (or at least most well know) out there when I was in the business was FX Concepts. They gave back their customers money a year or two ago because they couldn't make money trading FX.

Give yourself some credit guys, if your making money be proud of yourself's....if not then you have to keep at it if you truly love it."

--- 帖子 #1492 ---
EU was a 20 pip trade right from the start, you should either not have taken the trade or you should have taken scalp profit at the rising TL which was also S&R and the 50% Retr. The EU had set up a Triangle you should have been looking for a Breakout or as I said, a scalp within the Triangle.

EJ you entered far too late as you already accepted . You had a small Pin Bar off Falling TL PA had been tracking the TL down. A 123 with the Pin Bar forming the 3 point. TDI and Stochs showing downward momentum, again EJ had formed a Triangle and the 123 was part of the Breakout.

If you zoom out you would see all of this clearly. There is no benefit to zooming into a chart, unless you need glasses, you only see part of the picture. look at the chart attached you can see much more when you keep it zoomed out.

As for getting better exits.

1. Plan your Trade. Map out what you think price will do and plan your exits accordingly. See chart.

2. Take Partial Profits, so if you have got it wrong you have at least banked some pips.

3. Move SL to B/E as soon as you can, this takes away the fear of losing which is the main cause of closing out a trade to soon, yes you can be taken out more often, but, you can always enter again. I do not have losses I have Break evens. I no longer kick myself for getting taken out of a trade because I know there will always be another one.

4. Pick your trades, This is part of number 1. You do not have to be in the market all the time to win. This requires patience and discipline.

EDIT. Forgot to add. I am not telling you off! On the contrary. Yesterday you made a very nice profit so do not let me or any one else put you down. You had no losses you exited before that could happen. Well done.

--- 帖子 #1518 ---
Joe Dinapoli's said: "Don't use an Oscillator to price divergence as an entry technique, unless you have an excellent means of filtering it. Even for the best of Oscillators this can, and often does, spell disaster, particularly for the new participant. Price and Oscillator divergences abound, and the market continues to stop out the divergence players. Looking back in time, you're sure to find divergences that work, but when you're going forward in time, as in real trading, the accuracy of this technique just isn't there."

--- 帖子 #1519 ---
So are you saying, or rather Mr Dinapoli, that what I have been doing for the last 10 years is actually misguided? and that all the divergences I have ever traded have only been successful due to other circumstances?

--- 帖子 #1529 ---
The attached 1Hr chart hopefully makes it obvious why I took only short trades. The 2nd 15m chart shows why I went long on the 30th May. That should be obvious also. Here is the post that went with it.
http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...40#post7503040

My working day is 9.00 till 5.00, so if a divergence forms at 2.00am I will be in bed asleep. The problem with looking at charts is that they are 24hr, we on the other hand are not, so when back testing you should "always" keep this in mind. Try to look at the market in your time frame this way you will have a more realistic expectation of what you can achieve.

I tried to explain my method of drawing S&R lines here. http://www.forexfactory.com/showthre...27#post7457327

All I can add to that is, I look at the open/close of the candles more than I do the High/Low. The best way to see this is to look at one of my charts, make a note of the Price at which I have drawn a level, put it on one of your charts and then follow it left noting where Price makes contact with the Level, also look at a HTF & LTF, Repeat for other levels until you get the idea, after that it is only time until your eyes see the levels easily.

Hope it helps.

PS. I am still on Holiday so forgive me if I do not reply promptly.

--- 帖子 #1543 ---
EU. ECB Int Rate + Draghi Conference. +25 +10 +10. First entry was a "sentiment Entry" prior to the announcement, no change expected in Int Rate = Euro Negative, but the market did not react so I left it running until the Draghi conference this took price down to my TP for +25. next 2 trades were scalps following comments, using the momentum created by buyers coming in looking for the stops at 1.3390 and the prior sellers getting out. News Conferences are notoriously difficult to trade and are best left alone unless you understand the effects that the rhetoric create in the market. Trade the news conferences after the event not during.

I will try and explain, but just not today, sorry.

--- 帖子 #1550 ---
Trading the News with Sentiment. Start with these 2 links, have a look through these 2 sites you should get an idea of what is involved in analysing the news to provide you with the Sentiment for each announcement.

This is at least a starting point.

When I have found something more I will post it for you, the difficulty is, that determining Sentiment is highly subjective and depends on the level of experience of the analyst. Kathy and Boris have been doing this for some time and even have an Asset Management division based around News Trading so it is fair to say that they have developed a fairly reliable model on which to base their assessments.

Hope it helps, for now.
Day Trading News | Forex Trading Room - Learn From and Chat With Real Traders | BK Forex

BK Asset Management | Kathy Lien, Boris Schlossberg, Managed Forex, Forex News

--- 帖子 #1592 ---
Yes and No. Technical Analysis is often right and often wrong. Some News moves the market and other news does not. Sometimes the market moves with Sentiment and some times it does the opposite. The one thing you can be sure of is that if you wait the chart will show you which way the market is going to go. (Note to me)

Best way I can answer is to show you what I ignored and what I got wrong.

My biggest mistake was that I completely missed off the Major S&R level at 1.3115, I mark up a separate Daily chart with nothing on it and then copy the levels onto my 1Hr charts, some how I missed this level, carelessness, sloppiness what ever you want to call it. If I had seen this I would not have taken the first entry. I also missed that price had reached the 200% Exp of the Daily 123 that started 16 july, and that the 3rd leg down of the last 3 was much smaller than the previous 2 indicating a change in momentum and possibly direction. The SMI was deeply OS.

Attached Image (click to enlarge)

The real crime occurred on the 2nd entry. The 2nd entry was a complete and utter cock up, a 5yr old with only 1 day of instruction would not have taken that one! Take a look at these charts they show every thing

--- 帖子 #1599 ---
Thanks for the vote of confidence, but I have to be hard on myself because there is no one else to kick me up the **s. It is when I get soft with myself that I make stupid mistakes. Every trade I make, win or lose gets analysed at the end of every day, I mark up the chart, highlite what I missed what I did not see, then the chart is saved and is placed in 1 of 2 folders. 1 folder is for the good charts where I did not miss any thing, that folder is quite small, folder no2 contains the charts where I missed stuff, this one is quite large  it is this folder that I go thru on a daily basis reminding myself what I did not see and in the process re-training my eyes to see these things without having to think about it!

This is the time that traders refer to as "Screen Time" not the hours spent watching the charts waiting for a trade.
